Treatment for stage II Posterior Tibial Tendon Insufficiency (PTTI):<br><br>{{c1::FDL transfer, calcaneal medial slide osteotomy +/- lateral column lengthening}}	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Stage II disease is substratified based on the degree of talonavicular uncoverage. LCL is added if there is &gt;40% or &gt;30 degrees&nbsp; (stage IIb) uncovering of the talar head as FDL transfer and medial slide osteotomy will not correct severe forefoot abduction. LCL is performed either through the calcaneocuboid joint or the anterior calcaneus.&nbsp;<br></span><br><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Reconstruction of Stage IIB deformity typically involves:&nbsp;</span><br><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">1) reconstruction of the arch (FDL transfer to medial navicular)&nbsp;</span><br><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">2) correction of hindfoot valgus (MCO). Although her hindfoot is supple, MCO is performed to protect the soft tissue arch reconstruction and prevent early failure&nbsp;</span><br><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">3) correct forefoot abduction (lateral column lengthening).&nbsp;</span><br><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">4) correct equinus (TAL or gastrocnemius recession).&nbsp;</span>"																DegenerativeConditions FootAndAnkle PosteriorTibialTendonInsufficiencyPTTI TendonConditions
A {{c1::Cotton}} osteotomy is a plantarflexion osteotomy to correct residual forefoot varus.	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>In acquired flat foot deformity, the hindfoot falls into valgus with compensatory varus developing in the forefoot. When performing <u>ORIF</u> of an <b>isolated femoral head fracture (Pipkin II)</b>, the <i>approach</i> should be {{c1::anterior}} and the <i>fixation</i> should be with {{c1::mini-frag screws}}.	"<div><br></div><div>Marecek et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/27490911/) authored a review article on femoral head fractures. They described these injuries as being generally associated with hip dislocations and require prompt reduction. <b>They noted that the surgical fixation of the femoral head is generally done through the direct anterior approach or via a surgical hip dislocation depending on associated injuries.</b> <b>The authors also discussed the importance of using mini-frag screws to avoid hardware prominence.</b> They also noted that while heterotopic ossification is a common finding after the anterior approach for these injuries, it is rarely proven to be symptomatic. <div>{{c1::Total hip arthroplasty}} is the <u>best long term solution </u>for <b>displaced femoral neck fractures (FNF)</b> in <u>active elderly patients</u>.</div>	"<br><div>THA has best pain relief, fewer reoperations, best survivorship and is most cost-effective but has longer operative/anesthetic time, blood loss, higher infection rate, and potential instability compared with hemiarthroplasty.&nbsp;</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>Yu et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/22395872/) performed a meta-analysis of randomized controlled trials to determine whether THA or hemiarthroplasty (HA) was superior. They found that THA had lower risk of reoperation (RR = 0.53), higher risk of dislocation (RR = 1.99), and higher functional scores at 1 and 4 years. There was no difference in mortality, infection and complication rates.</div>"																FemoralNeckFractures LowerExtremity ProximalFemur Trauma
<div>For <b>displaced femoral neck fractures</b>, <u>physiologically young patients</u> are treated with {{c1::internal fixation}} while <u>physiologically old patients</u> are treated with either {{c1::hemiarthroplasty}} (debilitated, less active patients) or {{c1::THA}} (more active patients, those with acetabular disease or preexisting inflammatory arthritis).&nbsp;</div>																	FemoralNeckFractures LowerExtremity ProximalFemur Trauma

"<div><br>Valgus intertrochanteric osteotomies function by making a vertical fracture more horizontal, converting shear into compressive forces. Classifying <b>proximal femur fractures</b> is easier if the patient is placed in {{c1::traction}} with {{c1::internal rotation}} positioning.	<br><div>Koval et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/18537778/) performed a study in which proximal femur fractures were classified with standard radiographs (AP pelvis, AP hip, cross-table lateral), followed by the addition of a physician-assisted view with traction and 15 degrees of internal rotation. The inclusion of the traction-internal rotation view led to increased agreement in classification between the authors, and was especially helpful for differentiating displaced femoral neck fractures versus stable intertrochanteric fractures.</div>																FemoralNeckFractures LowerExtremity ProximalFemur Trauma
When surgical treatment of a hip fracture is delayed {{c1::&gt;4 days::how many days?}}, the 30-day, 90-day, and 1-year mortality significantly increases.	<br><div>Moran et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/15741611/) studied 2660 elderly patients who underwent surgical treatment of a hip fracture to determine whether a delay in surgery affects postoperative mortality. The 30-day mortality for patients for whom the surgery had been delayed for more than 4 days was 10.7%, compared to 7.3% in those delayed 1-4 days. The group delayed &gt;4 days also had significantly increased mortality at 90 days and 1 year.</div>																FemoralNeckFractures LowerExtremity ProximalFemur Trauma

<div>The {{c1::tip-apex distance (TAD)}} as it relates to a <u>lag screw</u> in the <b>femoral head</b> is the <i>summation</i> of the <u>distance between</u> the <i>end of the screw</i> and the <u>apex</u> of the <b>femoral head</b> on <u>AP</u> and <u>lateral radiographs</u>.</div>	"<div><div><br><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-06-27 at 7.11.52 PM.png""><br></div></div>"																IntertrochantericFractures LowerExtremity ProximalFemur Trauma
<div>A TAD of &lt;{{c1::25}}mm has been shown to <u>minimize</u> the <i>risk</i> of <u>fixation cut-out</u> in <b>stable</b> and <b>unstable intertrochanteric hip fractures</b>.&nbsp;</div>	"<div><br>Baumgaertner et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/7608228/) examined factors leading to the failure of sliding hip screws (SHS) in the treatment of 198 intertrochanteric fractures. They determined that the TAD is a reproducible, standard measurement to predict SHS failure. The average TAD for successful fractures was 24mm while the average TAD for failures was 38mm. No screw with a TAD &lt;25mm failed.&nbsp;<br><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-06-27 at 7.11.52 PM.png""><br></div>"																IntertrochantericFractures LowerExtremity ProximalFemur Trauma

<b>Latissimus dorsi transfer</b> for <u>rotator cuff tears</u> is <i>appropriate in patients</i> with <u>irreparable cuff tears</u> of the {{c1::supraspinatus}} and {{c1::infraspinatus}}.	"<div>Irreparable rotator cuff tears</div>
<ol>
<li>Superior displacement of the humeral head (AHI&lt;5-7 mm) - acromio-humeral interval</li>
<li>Goutallier stage 3-4 of rotator cuff muscles</li>
<li>Increased duration of tear</li>
<li>Substantial ER weakness</li></ol><div>Gerber et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24196461/) performed a case series analysis of 67 patients with irreparable rotator cuff tears managed with latissimus dorsi transfer. Patients with an intact subscapularis demonstrated improvement in pain, range of motion and strength postoperatively, while no improvement was noted in patients with subscapularis deficiency. The authors conclude that latissimus dorsi transfer should not be performed in the setting of poor subscapularis function.</div>"																ImpingementAndRotatorCuff RotatorCuffTears ShoulderAndElbow::Shoulder ShoulderAndElbow

<b>Vertical ACL grafts</b> will provide {{c1::anteroposterior}} stability, but not {{c1::rotational}} stability.	"<div>Early arthroscopic single-incision transtibial ACL reconstruction often resulted in femoral tunnels which were at the top of the notch (12 o:clock position), rather than at the anatomic origin on the wall. To <u>prevent future leg-length discrepancies</u> in <i>children/adolescents</i> undergoing <b>ACL reconstruction</b>, a {{c1::physeal-sparing}} technique should be used.	"<div><br>When considering transphyseal ACL reconstruction techniques in skeletally immature patients, a horizontally oriented tunnel and interference screw has the greatest potential to cause tibial physeal injury.&nbsp;</div>
<div><br>Frosch et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/21035009/) evaluated the clinical outcomes and risks of anterior cruciate ligament (ACL) surgery in children and adolescents. They found that the overall rate of leg-length difference was significantly less with transphyseal reconstruction techniques than physeal-sparing.&nbsp;<br><br><img src=""Representation-of-different-pediatric-ACL-reconstruction-techniques-in-lateral-knee.png""><br></div>"																ACLTear LowerExtremity::Knee LowerExtremity::Knee::KneeAndSports LigamentInjury
What is the <u>most common cause</u>&nbsp;of <b>ACL reconstruction</b>&nbsp;failure?<br><br>{{c1::Tibial tunnel malpositioning}}	"<div><br>Failure following primary ACL reconstruction has been associated with surgical error in 65-75% of cases. Of these cases, tunnel malposition is the most common, accounting for 70% of the errors. Successful ACL reconstruction has been demonstrated with hamstring autograft as well as bone-patellar tendon bone autograft, quadriceps autograft and multiple allograft specimens. Appropriate rehabilitation is crucial for successful return to sport, but there is not a more frequent cause of failure than surgical error.&nbsp;<br><br>Ideal tunnel positioning below:<br><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-07-10 at 4.48.29 PM.png""><br></div>"																ACLTear LowerExtremity::Knee LowerExtremity::Knee::KneeAndSports LigamentInjury

Why does using a <u>skirted femoral head</u> for <b>THA</b> lead to <u>increased risk of hip impingement and dislocation</u>?<br><br>{{c1::Decreases head to neck ratio}}	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Barrack (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/12670135/)
looked at implant design and orientation and its role in hip impingement and
dislocations after THAs. Ways to minimize the risk of impingement and
dislocation included avoiding the use of skirted heads, maximing head-to-neck
ratio, and using chamfered acetabular liners whenever possible. With the use of
computer modeling studies, he found that optimal femoral component anteversion
is 10-20 degrees, while optimal acetabular component positioning is 10-20
degrees of anteversion and 45-55 degrees of abduction.</span></div><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-08-03 at 10.43.36 AM.png"">"																LowerExtremity::Hip::HipReconstruction Recon THAPrimaryTechniques THAStabilityTechniques

When treating <b><i>displaced </i>midshaft clavicle fractures</b>, do patients who receive <u>nonoperative</u> or <u>operative treatment</u> perform better?<br><br>{{c1::Operative}}	"<font color=""#333333""><br></font><div>The Canadian Orthopaedic Trauma Society (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/17200303/) randomized 132 patients to operative or nonoperative treatment for displaced middle-third clavicle fractures and followed them for 1 year. They found improved Constant and Dash scores in the operative fixation group at all time points. In the nonoperative group, they found a nonunion rate of ~14% and symptomatic malunion rate of ~18%. They concluded operative fixation of displaced middle-third clavicle fractures leads to improved functional outcomes and a lower rate of nonunion and symptomatic malunion when compared to nonoperative treatment at 1 year follow up.</div>"																MidshaftClavicleFractures ShoulderAndElbow::Shoulder Trauma UpperExtremity

Best method for wound irrigation:<br><br>{{c1::Saline::Abx/Saline}} solution applied by {{c1::low::high/low}} pressure gravity flow device.	"<div>In an animal model, Hassinger et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/16205133/) showed that high-pressure pulsatile lavage caused deeper penetration of bacteria and results in greater bacterial retention in soft tissue when compared with low-pressure lavage.</div>
<div>Owens et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/19122083/), in a sheep model of contaminated soft tissue, compared low and high pressure lavage with normal saline solution, bacitracin solution, castile soap, and benzalkonium chloride. At 48 hours the group treated by low pressure lavage and saline showed the lowest rebound in bacterial counts.</div>"																Evaluation GeneralTrauma OpenFracturesManagement Trauma

<u>Operative treatment</u> <i>indications</i> for <b>pediatric both bone forearm fractures</b> following <i>unsuccessful closed reduction</i>:<br><br>Children &lt;{{c2::10}} y/o: {{c1::Angulation &gt;15°, rotation &gt;45°}}<br><br>Children ≥{{c2::10}} y/o: {{c1::Angulation &gt;10°, rotation &gt;30°, bayonet apposition}}	13 y/o is cutoff. After that age they are too close to skeletal maturity and should be treated like adults.<br><br><div>Nooonan and Price (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/9689186/) provide guidelines for acceptable displacement of the radius and ulna. In fractures in any level in children less than 9 years of age, complete displacement, 15 degrees of angulation, and 45 degrees of malrotation are acceptable. In children age 9 or older, 30 degrees of malrotation is acceptable, with 10 degrees of angulation for proximal fractures and 15 degrees for more distal fractures. Complete bayonet apposition is acceptable as long as angulation does not exceed 20 degrees and the patient has at least 2 years of growth remaining.</div>																BothBoneForearmFracturePediatric Forearm::ForearmTrauma Pediatric::Pediatrics Pediatric::PediatricTrauma

What is the <u>difference in rates of union</u> for <b>pediatric both bone forearm fractures</b> when comparing <b>percutaneous/open IM nailing </b>vs <b>ORIF</b>?<br><br>{{c1::None}}	"<img src=""paste-5496f738c50d0bcfe3566a76282338e77961261f.jpg""><br><br><div>Reinhardt et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/18520274/) reviewed the outcomes of 31 pediatric both bone forearm fractures treated with intramedullary nailing (IMN) versus ORIF. The IMN group had shorter surgical time and less blood loss. No differences were found in rates of union, radial bow magnitude, or forearm rotation.</div>"																BothBoneForearmFracturePediatric Forearm::ForearmTrauma Pediatric::Pediatrics Pediatric::PediatricTrauma
Following <b>pediatric both bone forearm fracture</b>, should you place the patient in a short-arm or long-arm cast?<br><br>{{c1::Short-arm}}	"<div>As stated in the articles below, short arm casts for distal both bone forearm fractures are as effective as long arm casts; however, short arm casts have fewer complications associated with them.<br><br></div>
<div>Paneru et al. (https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2866844/) randomized 42 children aged 4-12 to an above-elbow group and 43 to a below-elbow group. They found that pain and swelling on the next day and one week after reduction was significantly higher in the above-elbow group. As well, patients in the above-elbow group were more likely to undergo a re-manipulation than the below-elbow group (9.5% vs. 2.3%, p=0.173).<br><br></div>
<div>Webb et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/16391244/) performed an RCT comparing short arm and long arm plaster casts for displaced distal both bone forearm fractures. They concluded that a well-molded short arm cast was equally as effective as a long-arm cast, and interfered less with daily activity. They stressed the need for proper cast molding, indicated by a lower cast index. The ideal cast index is less than 0.8.</div>"																BothBoneForearmFracturePediatric Forearm::ForearmTrauma Pediatric::Pediatrics Pediatric::PediatricTrauma

Nails with a(n) {{c1::increased::increased/decreased}} <u>radius of curvature</u> are <i>straighter</i>, and therefore more likely to perforate the anterior distal femur.	"<br><div><div>According to the study by Egol et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/15289685/), the average femoral anterior radius of curvature was 120 cm (+/- 36 cm), and currently available femoral nails have a greater radius of curvature (i.e. more straight). This mismatch has been shown to lead to an increased risk of perforation of the anterior distal femur as the nail is impacted into the canal.</div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span><img src=""1-s2.0-S0972978X14000294-gr2.jpg""><img src=""download-bf854d17058953eb8b3259452609db711ed0b3ad.jpg""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"																FemoralShaftFractures LowerExtremity ShaftAndDistalFemur Trauma
<b>Indomethacin therapy</b> {{c1::decreases::increases/decreases}} the risk of <i>heterotopic ossification</i>, but {{c1::increases::increases/decreases}} the risk of <i>delayed bone healing</i>.	<br><div>Indomethacin therapy has been shown to be an effective means of preventing HO formation, however literature has shown that it increases the risk of long bone and acetabular nonunion. Indomethacin works primarily by inhibiting IGF-1, which is a different mechanism from other NSAID's which typically inhibit the COX enzymes. IGF-1 is important for bone healing, and its inhibition may be a risk factor for delayed bone healing.</div>																FemoralShaftFractures LowerExtremity ShaftAndDistalFemur Trauma

"Following <b>tibial plateau fracture</b>, what <u>postoperative protocol</u> has the most beneficial effect on the <i>healing potential</i> of <u>surviving chondrocytes</u>?<br><br>{{c1::Gentle compressive loading of the affected joint
through early range of motion exercises}}"	<div>Irrgang et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/9785258/) provide guidelines for rehabilitation following surgical management of articular cartilage lesions of the knee. They state that after articular cartilage repair, exercises to enhance muscle function must be done in a manner which minimizes shear loading of the joint surfaces in the area of the lesion. The authors also discuss the benefits of gentle compressive loading and motion of the joint, and its positive effects on chondrocyte nutrition. Furthermore, they recommend a period of protected weight bearing as often being necessary, and that this should be followed by progressive loading of the joint.</div>																LowerExtremity::Knee LowerExtremity TibialPlateauFractures Trauma
"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">What <i>variable</i> will most significantly <u>increase rate of
degenerative arthritis</u> in the <u>long-term</u> following <b>ORIF</b>&nbsp;of a&nbsp;<b>tibial plateau fracture</b>?<br><br></span>{{c1::Alteration of limb mechanical axis}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">According to the study of plateau fractures with up to 27
year follow-up by Rademakers et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/17211262/),
malalignment of the limb by greater than 5 degrees tripled the rate of
degenerative osteoarthritis (27% v. 9%). Age at time of injury had no effect on
outcome; 31% had joint space narrowing but 64% of those knees were well
tolerated.&nbsp;</span></div>"																LowerExtremity::Knee LowerExtremity TibialPlateauFractures Trauma

since the fall. Radiographs shown below. Next step?<br><br>{{c1::Long leg cast application}}<br><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-05 at 6.40.49 AM.png""><br></div>"	"<div>-The clinical presentation is consistent with a toddler's fracture, which is treated with a long leg cast. Initial radiographs are often negative but follow-up radiographs may demonstrate a healing periosteal reaction.</div>
<div>-Long leg cast is placed for 3-4 weeks.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>-Halsey et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/11242240/)Â&nbsp;retrospectively reviewed toddler's fracture with negative radiographs on the presumption that this diagnosis, despite negative radiographs, is appropriate when the history and physical examination are consistent with the diagnosis. They found that 41% of toddler's fractures were confirmed on follow-up radiographs and that no particular characteristics could predict the outcome when comparing the children who demonstrated a toddler's fracture with those who did not. They concluded that to avoid delay in the treatment of toddler's fracture, a long-leg cast should be applied to those children with a history of an acute injury, inability to walk or limp, no constitutional signs, and negative radiographs.</div>"																Pediatric::Pediatrics Pediatric::PediatricTrauma TibiaAndAnkleTrauma TibialShaftFracturesPediatric

<i>Two (2)</i> types of <b>scoliosis</b> in patients with <b>neurofibromatosis</b>:<br><br>{{c1::Idiopathic (non-dystrophic)<br>Dystrophic}}	<div><br>Scoliosis and kyphosis are commonly seen in patients with neurofibromatosis. Non-dystrophic forms of scoliosis can be treated similarly to adolescent idiopathic scoliosis (AIS) not otherwise associated with NF. However, dystrophic scoliosis is resistant to bracing and often requires early surgical intervention. There is a known association of NF with dural ectasia, or a widening of the dural sac. A preoperative MRI of the spinal axis must be done preoperatively to rule out this abnormality and avoid potential complications. Preoperative MRI can also help to evaluate for neurofibromas of the cord or nerve roots.</div>																Neurofibromatosis Pediatric::PediatricConditions Pediatric::Pediatrics TibialBowing
In a patient with <b>neurofibromatosis </b>and associated <b>dystrophic</b> <b>scoliosis</b>, it is important to order a preoperative MRI to evaluate for {{c1::dural ectasia}}.	"<div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-06 at 6.50.23 AM.png""><br><br><font color=""#333333"">Scoliosis

The {{c1::Tanner-Whitehouse III RUS}} method of <u>skeletal maturity determination</u> is the <i>most accurate</i> method, but is time consuming.	"<div>-The Tanner-Whitehouse III method specifically uses the distal radial and ulnar epiphyses and the metacarpal and phalangeal epiphyses of the first, third, and fifth digits for determination of skeletal age. In contrast, the Risser sign refers to the amount of calcification of the human pelvis as a measure of maturity. While the Tanner-Whitehouse method is more time consuming, it provides a better assessment of maturity and prognosis determination for curve progression in idiopathic scoliosis.</div>

studied the predictive values of the ‘cover-up’ test in differentiating between
physiologic and pathologic bowing. The test is performed with the patient
supine and lower extremities fully extended with the patellas pointing straight
up. One hand is holding the ankle and the other is placed perpendicular to the
long axis of the tibia to ‘cover-up’ the middle. Physiologic bowing is
indicated by a valgus proximal tibia, while a Blount's patient will have a
neutral or varus proximal tibia.<br><br><img src=""paste-00803d06adfee3e51306479c0458948c755a6ab9.jpg""><br></div>"																InfantileBlountsDiseaseTibiaVara Pediatric::PediatricConditions Pediatric::Pediatrics VarusAndValgusDeformities

<b>Cerebral Palsy</b> is classified by {{c1::physiology}} or {{c1::anatomy}}.	"<br><div>Physiology:</div>
<div>Spastic: increased muscle tone and
hyperreflexia with slow restricted movements secondary to simultaneous
contracture of agonists and antagonists. This is the most common form. CP
spasticity is characterized by increased muscle tone, hyperreflexia and tone
that increases with velocity.</div>
<div>Athetosis: constant succession of slow,
writhing involuntary motions Ataxia: Inability to coordinate muscles for
voluntary movement. Characterized by wide-based gait.</div>
<div>Mixed: combination of spastic and
athetosis with total body involvement.</div>
<div>&nbsp;</div>
<div>Anatomy:</div>
<div>Hemiplegia: Affecting both limbs on one
side, arm usually worse than leg.</div>
<div>Diplegia: Affecting right and left side
equally. Minimal spasticity may be present in upper limbs, but lower limb
spasticity predominates. IQ may be near normal.</div>
<div>Paraplegia: Affecting both legs,
sparing of arms.Quadriplegia:
Both legs and both arms. Associated with low IQ and higher mortality.</div>
<div>Monoplegia: Affecting only one limb.</div>"																CerebralPalsy CerebralPalsy::CerebralPalsyGeneral Pediatric::Pediatrics Pediatric::PediatricSyndromes
"In patients with <b>Cerebral Palsy</b>, strong tone in hip {{c1::adductor}} and {{c1::flexor}} muscles lead to
scissoring and predisposes to hip subluxation and dislocation (commonly posterior and superior)."																	CerebralPalsy CerebralPalsy::CerebralPalsyHipConditions Pediatric::Pediatrics Pediatric::PediatricSyndromes

"<div>What <i>medication</i> is <u>recommended</u> to <i>prevent</i> the incidence of
<b>reflex sympathetic dystrophy (RSD)</b> following <b>distal radius fracture</b>?<br><br>{{c1::Vitamin C}}<br></div>"	"<div>-AAOS 2010 clinical practice guidelines recommend this
postoperatively</div>
<div>-500 mg once daily for 50 days</div>
<div>-Zollinger et al.
(https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/17606778/) performed a double-blinded
randomized controlled trial of 427 wrist fractures, allocating patients to
receive placebo or 200, 500, or 1500mg of vitamin C for 50 days. The authors
found that in the vitamin C group, the incidence of CRPS was 2.4%, while it was
10.1% in the placebo group. They showed no difference in relative risk between
the 500mg and 1500mg groups. The authors concluded that Vitamin C reduces the
prevalence of CRPS and a daily dose of 500mg for 50 days is recommended.</div>"																DistalRadius Forearm Trauma UpperExtremity

How are outcomes of patients with an accompanying ulnar styloid fracture with stable fixation of a distal radius fracture? (Compared to no ulnar styloid fracture)<br><br>{{c1::No difference}}	"<div>Kim et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/20048089/)
evaluated 138 patients who underwent surgical treatment of an unstable distal
radial fracture, without fixation of an associated ulnar styloid fracture if
present. Postoperative evaluation included measurement of grip strength and
wrist range of motion; calculation of the modified Mayo wrist score; as well as
testing for instability of the distal radioulnar joint at a mean of 19
postoperatively. They did not find a significant relationship between wrist
functional outcomes and ulnar styloid fracture level or the amount of
displacement.</div>"																DistalRadius Forearm Trauma UpperExtremity

<div>{{c1::Degree of displacement seen on postoperative CT}} has been shown to <i>most closely correlate</i> with <u>outcomes</u> following <u>ORIF</u> of <b>posterior wall fractures</b>.</div>	"<div>Moed et al.
(https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/12637440/) evaluated the results of 67 patients
who underwent ORIF of a posterior wall fractures by assessing the accuracy of
postoperative AP pelvis, obturator oblique films, iliac oblique films, and CT
scans. They found that postoperative pelvic CT scan was the most accurate way
to judge final fracture reduction and was able to pick up residual fracture
displacements that were not seen on postoperative plain radiographs. They
concluded that the accuracy of reduction as assessed on postoperative CT scan
was the most reliable indicator of clinical outcomes.</div>"																AcetabularFractures Acetabulum PelvisTrauma Trauma

<div><u>Antegrade intramedullary (IM) nailing</u> of <b>humeral shaft fractures</b> has been found to be associated with {{c1::increased::increased/decreased}} complication rates when <i>compared</i> with <u>open reduction and internal fixation (ORIF)</u>.</div>	"<div>Heineman et al. (2010) (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/20170424/) conducted a meta-analysis of prospective randomized studies comparing IM nailing with ORIF for humeral shaft fractures. The authors found no significant difference between the two treatment modalities for either their primary outcome (complications) or any of the secondary outcomes (nonunion, infection, nerve palsy, re-operation).<br><br></div>
<div>Heineman et al. (2012) (https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3369163/) have recently conducted an update on their meta-analysis to include more recent randomized studies. With the inclusion of these newer studies the author found a statistically significant increase in total complication rate with the use of IM nailing compared with ORIF.</div>"																Humerus::HumeralShaftFractures Humerus Trauma UpperExtremity

<i>Early decompression</i> has been shown to {{c1::increase::increase/decrease}} the <u>likelihood of neurologic recovery</u> in both <b>complete</b> and <b>incomplete spinal cord injuries</b>.	<div><br>Fehlings et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/22384132/) performed a multicenter prospective cohort study on the timing of intervention for spinal cord injuries. They found improved neurological outcome for patients with complete or incomplete spinal cord injuries that were decompressed within 24 hours compared to those that were decompressed at a later time. Additionally, they found no increased risk of mortality or complications for patients who underwent early surgical intervention.</div>																Spine::SpinalCordInjuries Spine::SpinalCordInjury Spine Trauma

{{c1::Posterior cervical fusion}} is the <u>treatment of choice</u> for <u><i>symptomatic</i></u> <b>cervical pseudoarthrosis</b> following <b>anterior cervical diskectomy and fusion</b>.	<br>Even though there are increased complications with the posterior approach, there are substantially increased rates of fusion with lower revision surgery rate.<br><br><div>*The study by Carreon et al (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/16517386/) is a retrospective case series that compared posterior cervical fusion versus revision anterior surgery for the treatment of a symptomatic pseudoarthrosis. They found a second revision surgery for persistent nonunion was required in 44% of patients in the anterior revision group, and only 2% of the patients in the posterior revision group. Therefore, they argue that despite increased blood loss, longer postoperative hospitalization, and an increased complication rate, posterior cervical fusion is a better treatment option due to higher fusion rates and a decrease in revision surgery rates.</div>																CervicalConditions CervicalRadiculopathy Spine Spine::SpineDegenerative

<div>{{c1::Power}} is the <u>ability of a study</u> <i>to detect</i> the <b>difference between two interventions</b> <i>if one exists</i>.</div>	<br><div>*The power of a statistical test is correlated to the magnitude of the treatment effect, the designated type I (alpha) and type II (beta) error rates, and the sample size n. The power is equal to (1-beta) whereby beta is the false negative rate.</div>																BasicScience ClinicalScience ClinicalStudies StatisticDefinitions
<div>A {{c1::Bonferroni correction}} is a <u>post-hoc statistical correction</u> made to <b>P values</b> when <i>several dependent or independent statistical tests</i> are being performed <i>simultaneously</i> on a <u>single data set</u>.</div>	<br>*To perform a Bonferroni correction, divide the critical P value (alpha level) by the number of comparisons being made. For example, if 10 hypotheses are being tested, the new critical P value would be (alpha level)/10. The statistical power of the study is then calculated based on this modified P value.																BasicScience ClinicalScience ClinicalStudies StatisticDefinitions
{{c1::Incidence}}: number of NEW cases of a disease diagnosed during a specific time period per unit measurement of population.<br><br>{{c1::Prevalence}}: total number of cases of the disease in the population at a given time. "<div><u>Pathophysiology of metastasis to bone:</u></div>
<div><br></div>
<div>{{c1::E cadherin cell adhesion molecule (CAM)}} on tumor cells modulates release from primary tumor into bloodstream.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>{{c2::Chemokine ligand 12 (CXCL12)}} in the stromal cells of bone marrow acts as homing chemokine to certain tumor cells and promote targeting of bone.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>Uses {{c3::matrix metalloproteinases (MMPs)}} to invade the basement membrane and ECP</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>Induces angiogenesis via {{c4::vascular endothelial growth factor (VEGF)}} expression</div>"																	Bones::BoneTumors MetastaticDisease MetastaticDiseaseOfExtremity pathology
"<div><u>Pathophysiology of lytic vs osteoblastic metastatic lesions:</u></div>
<div><br></div>
<div>Lytic: Tumor cells secrete {{c1::PTHrP}} which stimulates {{c1::RANKL}} from osteoblasts, which binds to RANK receptors on osteoclast precursor cells. These osteoclasts then cause bony destruction.</div>
<div><br></div>
<div>Osteoblastic: Tumor cells secrete {{c2::endothelin-1 (ET-1)}} which binds to {{c2::endothelia A receptor (ETAR)}} on osteoblasts to stimulate them.</div>"																	Bones::BoneTumors MetastaticDisease MetastaticDiseaseOfExtremity pathology
<div>{{c1::Metastatic carcinoma}} is the <u>most common</u> cause of a <b>destructive bone lesion</b> in <i>older adults</i>.</div>																	Bones::BoneTumors MetastaticDisease MetastaticDiseaseOfExtremity pathology
<div>{{c1::Preoperative embolization}} is indicated for <b>renal cell</b> or <b>thyroid carcinoma</b> because these cancers are <u>very vascular</u>.</div>																	Bones::BoneTumors MetastaticDisease MetastaticDiseaseOfExtremity pathology

"<div>69 y/o man presents with known metastatic lung cancer and the following pathological fracture after falling from standing height. Best treatment?<br><br><div>{{c1::Cephalomedullary nail}}</div><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-11-30 at 2.07.10 PM.png""><br></div>"	<div>*Based on the location of the lesion, neither a total hip arthroplasty nor a hemiarthroplasty would be appropriate - unless a cemented long stem which bypasses the defect is available as a treatment option. A sliding hip screw is not an appropriate treatment choice because of the subtrochanteric nature of the fracture and the fact that the sliding hip screw does not biomechanically address subtrochanteric fractures. As this patient has significant bone loss, a dynamically locked nail is at risk of shortening, and only the statically locked nail will provide resistance to the torsional stress and angular displacement.</div>																Bones::BoneTumors MetastaticDisease MetastaticDiseaseOfExtremity pathology
"<div>51 y/o F with metastatic breast cancer presents with the following pathologic fracture. Biopsy confirms metastatic breast cancer. Best next step?<br><br><div>{{c1::Intramedullary nailing, radiation therapy to the entire femur, and chemotherapy}}</div><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-11-30 at 2.32.26 PM.png""><br></div>"	<div>*Due to the process of placing the intramedullary nail, the treating surgeon contaminates the ENTIRE femur with breast cancer. The surrounding area is already contaminated with tumor cells from the fracture, however. While the intramedullary nail will stabilize the pathological fracture, it does nothing to control the local progression of breast cancer in this patient's leg. Local radiotherapy will not only improve the local control of disease but it will palliate the patient's cancer related pain.</div>																Bones::BoneTumors MetastaticDisease MetastaticDiseaseOfExtremity pathology

<div><b>Medical negligence</b> <i>comprises</i> <u>four elements</u>: <br><br><b>Duty:</b> {{c1::Duty of the physician is to provide care equal to the same standard of care ordinarily executed by surgeons in the same medical specialty.}}<br><br><b>Breach of duty:</b> {{c2::Breach of duty occurs when action or failure to act deviates from the standard of care.}}<br><br><b>Causation:</b>&nbsp;{{c3::Causation is present when it is demonstrated that failure to meet the standard of care was the direct cause of the patient's injuries.<br>}}</div><div><br><b>Damages:</b> {{c4::Damages are monies awarded as compensation for injuries sustained as the result of medical negligence.}}</div>																	BasicScience ClinicalScience LegalConsiderationsInOrthopaedicPractice PracticeManagement

"<div>{{c1::Creep}}
is the tendency of a solid material to move slowly or deform permanently under
the influence of stresses.</div>"	"<div>*Creep is an undesirable property of orthopaedic bio-materials because they
release frictional forces necessary to maintain rigid internal fixation. In
total hip arthroplasty polyethylene liners, creep is the plastic deformation of
the acetabular liner that occurs due to loading without the production of wear
debris or particles.</div>"																BasicScience MaterialProperties MaterialScience MSKScience
"<div><b>PMMA</b>,
or <b>bone cement</b>, has a <u>Young’s modulus</u> between {{c1::cortical}} and {{c1::cancellous}} bone.</div>"	"<div><br>*PMMA, or bone cement, is frequently used in joint replacement surgery, tumor
surgery, and spine surgery. Bone cements are provided as two-component
materials, a powder and a liquid. The powder usually contains a polymer,
benzoyl peroxide (initiator), and barium sulfate (radio-opacifier). The liquid
usually contains a monomer, DMPT (accelerator), and hydroquinone (stabilizer).
The two components are mixed and a free radical polymerization occurs when the
initiator is mixed with the accelerator.</div>"																BasicScience MaterialProperties MaterialScience MSKScience

How should RA patients who are on TNF-alpha inhibitors be managed perioperatively?<br><br>{{c1::Discontinue TNF-alpha inhibitor due to increased risk of infection}}	<div>Saleh et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/26271759/) reviewed the perioperative management of RA patients. They note that patients that are maintained on etanercept perioperatively have a significantly increased rate of perioperative infection. The authors discuss recommendations that etanercept be held at least one half-life prior to surgery and in some instances up to 4-5 half-lives before surgery. They recommend restarting the medication at 2 weeks post-operatively so long as the surgical sites are healing uneventfully.</div>																BasicScience RheumatoidArthritis SystematicArthropathies SystematicDisease

<div>86 y/o F suffers a comminuted bicolumnar distal humerus fracture. What is the most appropriate treatment for this patient?<br><br><div>{{c1::Total elbow arthroplasty}}</div></div>	"<div>*McKee et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/18823799/) peformed a randomized controlled trial of 42 patients comparing ORIF to TEA. Patients who had the TEA had better Mayo elbow scores from 3 months until 2 years postoperatively, but DASH scores were only better in the TEA group for the 1st 6 months (equal thereafter). Reoperation rates were not statistically different, but note was made of a 25% intraoperative conversion rate from ORIF to TEA after randomization. They conclude that this elderly population appears to adjust well to elbow limitations regardless of treatment.<br><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-01-11 at 5.02.31 PM.png""><br></div>"																DistalHumerusFractures Humerus Trauma UpperExtremity

"<div>How do you choose between <b>radial head ORIF</b> vs. <b>arthroplasty</b> in the setting of <b>terrible triad of the elbow</b>?<br><br></div>
<div>ORIF - {{c1::Non-comminuted fxs with &lt;40% articular surface involvement}}</div>
<div>Arthroplasty - {{c1::Comminuted fxs (&gt;3 pieces)}}</div>"	<div>*For the radial head fracture, cannot perform a simple excision. Ring et al. (https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/11940613/) reviewed 11 terrible triad injuries including 7 of which had the radial head surgically addressed and 4 of which had undergone radial head excision. The authors found that all four patients who underwent radial head excision dislocated after surgery. Only four patients had a satisfactory result, and all of these had fixation of the radial head, two requiring concomitant repair of the lateral ulnar collateral ligament (LUCL). The authors concluded that terrible triad injuries were unstable, prone to redislocation and that radiocapitellar contact is critical for ulnohumeral stability.</div>																Elbow TerribleTriadInjuryofElbow Trauma UpperExtremity

They note that complications and secondary procedures (treatment of infection, nonunion, malunion, prominent implant removal) were more frequent in LCP than ABP patients.</div>"																DistalFemurFractures LowerExtremity ShaftAndDistalFemur Trauma
"<div>Following fixation of a <b>distal femur fracture</b>, to ensure that the <u>intercondylar screws</u> are <i>contained within the bone</i> and are of <i>appropriate length</i>, it’s important to get which <u>additional fluoroscopic view</u>?<br></div>
<div><br>{{c1::AP with leg in 30° internal rotation}}</div>"	"<div>*Hardware irritation is a common post-operative complication of distal femoral plate fixation. Two common sites of pain are laterally where the iliotibial band is in contact with the plate, and medially where intercondylar screws may penetrate the cortex if they are of inappropriate length. Iliotibial irritation most commonly presents with activities requiring knee flexion and extension. It is important to remember that the lateral metaphysis of the distal femur is angulated 10 degrees from the sagittal plane, and the medial metaphysis is angulated 25 degrees from the sagittal plane. Therefore, if a straight AP view is obtained, a distal screw can appear to be inside the bone even if it is too long. In order to assess the exact length of the screw, one must obtain an AP view with 30° internal rotation of the lower extremity.&nbsp;<br><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-02-14 at 11.50.56 AM.png""><br></div>"																DistalFemurFractures LowerExtremity ShaftAndDistalFemur Trauma

<div>When performing a {{c1::saline load}} test to evaluate for a <u>traumatic arthrotomy</u>, a <i>minimum of 155 mL</i> is needed to obtain <i>95% diagnostic accuracy</i>.</div>	"<div>A saline load test is commonly utilized to evaluate for intraarticular penetration of superficial lacerations (traumatic arthrotomies). <div>In patients with <b>scapular fractures</b>, what <b>other fracture</b> is <u>most commonly observed</u>?<br><br><div>{{c1::Rib fracture}}</div></div>	<div>*Baldwin et al. (</span>https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/12902784/)&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">compared open reduction and internal fixation (ORIF) with total elbow arthroplasty (TEA) for intraarticular distal humerus fractures in women older than 65 years of age. Only difference between single row and double row rotator cuff repairs:<br><br>{{c1::Lower retear rate for double row repair}}	*DeHaan et al. performed a systematic review of prosepective level I or II studies that compared the efficacy of single-row RCR versus double-row RCR. The authors found that the functional ASES, Constant, and UCLA outcome scores revealed no difference between the 2 groups. The authors did note that the total retear rate, which included both complete and partial re-rears, was 43.1% for the single-row RCR and 27.2% for the double-row RCR (P = .057). The authors concluded that double-row RCR revealed a trend toward a lower radiographic proven re-tear rate, although the data did not reach statistical significance.
